This flag deals with the fact that Terraform\n   322→// Core uses a specialized graph node type for destroying; only that\n   323→// specialized node should set \"destroying\" to true.\n   324→//\n   325→// The following table shows the simplification behavior:\n   326→//\n   327→//\tAction    Destroying?   New Action\n   328→//\t--------+-------------+-----------\n   329→//\tCreate    true          NoOp\n   330→//\tDelete    false         NoOp\n   331→//\tReplace   true          Delete\n   332→//\tReplace   false         Create\n   333→//\n   334→// For any combination not in the above table, the Simplify just returns the\n   335→// receiver as-is.\n   336→func (rc *ResourceInstanceChange) Simplify(destroying bool) *ResourceInstanceChange {\n   337→\tif destroying {\n   338→\t\tswitch rc.Action {\n   339→\t\tcase Delete:\n   340→\t\t\t// We'll fall out and just 349→\t\t\t\t\tBefore:          rc.Before,\n   350→\t\t\t\t\tAfter:           cty.NullVal(rc.Before.Type()),\n   351→\t\t\t\t\tImporting:       rc.Importing,\n   352→\t\t\t\t\tGeneratedConfig: rc.GeneratedConfig,\n   353→\t\t\t\t},\n   354→\t\t\t}\n   355→\t\tdefault:\n   356→\t\t\treturn &ResourceInstanceChange{\n   357→\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n   358→\t\t\t\tDeposedKey:   rc.DeposedKey,\n   359→\t\t\t\tPrivate:      rc.Private,\n   360→\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr,\n   361→\t\t\t\tChange: Change{\n   362→\t\t\t\t\tAction:          NoOp,\n   363→\t\t\t\t\tBefore:          rc.Before,\n   364→\t\t\t\t\tAfter:           rc.Before,\n   365→\t\t\t\t\tImporting:       rc.Importing,\n   366→\t\t\t\t\tGeneratedConfig: rc.GeneratedConfig,\n   367→\t\t\t\t},\n   368→\t\t\t}\n   369→\t\t}\n   370→\t} else {\n   371→\t\tswitch rc.Action {\n   372→\t\tcase Delete:\n   373→\t\t\treturn &ResourceInstanceChange{\n   374→\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n   375→\t\t\t\tDeposedKey:   rc.DeposedKey,\n   376→\t\t\t\tPrivate:      rc.Private,\n   377→\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr,\n   378→\t\t\t\tChange: Change{\n   379→\t\t\t\t\tAction: rc.GeneratedConfig,\n   384→\t\t\t\t},\n   385→\t\t\t}\n   386→\t\tcase CreateThenDelete, DeleteThenCreate:\n   387→\t\t\treturn &ResourceInstanceChange{\n   388→\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n   389→\t\t\t\tDeposedKey:   rc.DeposedKey,\n   390→\t\t\t\tPrivate:      rc.Private,\n   391→\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr,\n   392→\t\t\t\tChange: Change{\n   393→\t\t\t\t\tAction:          Create,\n   394→\t\t\t\t\tBefore:          cty.NullVal(rc.After.Type()),\n   395→\t\t\t\t\tAfter:           rc.After,\n   396→\t\t\t\t\tImporting:       rc.Importing,\n   397→\t\t\t\t\tGeneratedConfig: rc.GeneratedConfig,\n   398→\t\t\t\t},\n   399→\t\t\t}\n   400→\t\t}\n   401→\t}\n   402→\n   403→\t// If we fall out here then our change is already simple enough.\n   404→\treturn rc\n   405→}\n   406→\n   407→// ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason allows for some extra user-facing\n   408→// reasoning for why a particular change action was chosen for a particular\n   409→// resource instance.\n   410→//\n   411→// This only represents sufficient detail to give a suitable explanation to\n   412→// an end-user, and mustn't be used for any real decision-making The caller should have dealt\n   614→\t// with those somehow and replaced them with unmarked placeholders before\n   615→\t// writing the value into the state.\n   616→\tunmarkedBefore, marksesBefore := c.Before.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n   617→\tunmarkedAfter, marksesAfter := c.After.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n   618→\tsensitiveAttrsBefore, unsupportedMarksesBefore := marks.PathsWithMark(marksesBefore, marks.Sensitive)\n   619→\tsensitiveAttrsAfter, unsupportedMarksesAfter := marks.PathsWithMark(marksesAfter, marks.Sensitive)\n   620→\tif len(unsupportedMarksesBefore) != 0 {\n   621→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\n   622→\t\t\t\"prior value %s: can't serialize value marked with %#v (this is a bug in Terraform)\",\n   623→\t\t\ttfdiags.FormatCtyPath(unsupportedMarksesBefore[0].Path),\n   624→\t\t\tunsupportedMarksesBefore[0].Marks,\n   625→\t\t)\n   626→\t}\n   627→\tif len(unsupportedMarksesAfter) != 0 {\n   628→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\n   629→\t\t\t\"new value %s: can't serialize value marked with %#v (this is a bug in Terraform)\",\n   630→\t\t\ttfdiags.FormatCtyPath(unsupportedMarksesAfter[0].Path),\n   631→\t\t\tunsupportedMarksesAfter[0].Marks,\n   632→\t\t)\n   633→\t}\n   634→\n   635→\tbeforeDV, err := NewDynamicValue(unmarkedBefore, ty)\n   636→\tif err != nil {\n   637→\t\treturn nil, err\n   638→\t}\n   639→\tafterDV, err := NewDynamicValue(unmarkedAfter, ty)\n   640→\tif err != nil {\n   641→\t\treturn nil, err\n   642→\t}\n   643→\n   644→\treturn &ChangeSrc{\n   645→\t\tAction:               c.Action,\n   646→\t\tBefore:               beforeDV,\n   647→\t\tAfter:                afterDV,\n   648→\t\tBeforeSensitivePaths: sensitiveAttrsBefore,\n   649→\t\tAfterSensitivePaths:  sensitiveAttrsAfter,\n   650→\t\tImporting:            c.Importing.Encode(),\n   651→\t\tGeneratedConfig:      c.GeneratedConfig,\n   652→\t}, nil\n   653→}\n   654→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Returns nil if no changes are\n// planned.\nfunc (c *Changes) OutputValues(parent addrs.ModuleInstance, module addrs.ModuleCall) []*OutputChange {\n\tvar res []*OutputChange\n\n\tfor _, oc := range ResourceInstanceChange describes a change to a particular resource instance\n// object.\ntype ResourceInstanceChange struct {\n\t// Addr is the absolute address of the resource instance that the change\n\t// will apply to.\n\tAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n\t// PrevRunAddr is the absolute address that this resource instance had at\n\t// the conclusion of a previous run.\n\t//\n\t// This will typically be the same as Addr, but can be different if the\n\t// previous resource instance was subject to a \"moved\" block that we\n\t// handled in the process of creating this plan.\n\t//\n\t// For the initial creation of a resource instance there isn't really any\n\t// meaningful \"previous run address\", but PrevRunAddr will still be set\n\t// equal to Addr in that case in order to simplify logic elsewhere which\n\t// aims to detect and react to the movement of instances between addresses.\n\tPrevRunAddr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n\t// DeposedKey is the identifier for a deposed object associated with the\n\t// given instance, or states.NotDeposed if this change applies to the\n\t// current object.\n\t//\n\t// A Replace change for a resource with create_before_destroy set will\n\t// create a new DeposedKey temporarily during replacement. In that case,\n\t// DeposedKey in the plan is always states.NotDeposed, representing that\n\t// the current object is being replaced with the deposed.\n\tDeposedKey states.DeposedKey\n\n\t// Provider is the address of the provider configuration that was used\n\t// to plan this change, and thus the configuration that must also be\n\t// used to apply it.\n\tProviderAddr addrs.AbsProviderConfig\n\n\t// Change is an embedded description of the change.\n\tChange\n\n\t// ActionReason is an optional extra indication of why we chose the\n\t// action recorded in Change.Action for this particular resource instance.\n\t//\n\t// This is an approximate mechanism only for the purpose of explaining the\n\t// plan to end-users in the UI and is not to be used for any\n\t// decision-making during the apply step; if apply behavior needs to vary\n\t// depending on the \"action reason\" then the information for that decision\n\t// must be recorded more precisely elsewhere for that purpose.\n\t//\n\t// Sometimes there might be more than one reason for choosing a particular\n\t// action. In that case, it's up to the codepath making that decision to\n\t// decide which value would provide the most relevant explanation to the\n\t// end-user and return that. It's not a goal of this field to represent\n\t// fine details about the planning process.\n\tActionReason ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n\n\t// RequiredReplace is a set of paths that caused the change action to be\n\t// Replace rather than Update. Always nil if the change action is not\n\t// Replace.\n\t//\n\t// This is retained only for UI-plan-rendering purposes and so it does not\n\t// currently survive a round-trip through a saved plan file.\n\tRequiredReplace cty.PathSet\n\n\t// Private allows a provider to stash any extra data that is opaque to\n\t// Terraform that relates to this change. Terraform will save this\n\t// byte-for-byte and return it to the provider in the apply call.\n\tPrivate []byte\n}\n\n// Encode produces a variant of the reciever that has its change values\n// serialized so it can be written to a plan file. Pass the implied type of the\n// corresponding resource type schema for correct operation.\nfunc (rc *ResourceInstanceChange) Encode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceChangeSrc, error) {\n\tcs, err := rc.Change.Encode(ty)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\tprevRunAddr := rc.PrevRunAddr\n\tif prevRunAddr.Resource.Resource.Type == \"\" {\n\t\t// Suggests an old caller that hasn't been properly updated to\n\t\t// populate this yet.\n\t\tprevRunAddr = rc.Addr\n\t}\n\treturn &ResourceInstanceChangeSrc{\n\t\tAddr:            rc.Addr,\n\t\tPrevRunAddr:     prevRunAddr,\n\t\tDeposedKey:      rc.DeposedKey,\n\t\tProviderAddr:    rc.ProviderAddr,\n\t\tChangeSrc:       *cs,\n\t\tActionReason:    rc.ActionReason,\n\t\tRequiredReplace: rc.RequiredReplace,\n\t\tPrivate:         rc.Private,\n\t}, err\n}\n\nfunc (rc *ResourceInstanceChange) DeepCopy() *ResourceInstanceChange {\n\tif rc == nil {\n\t\treturn rc\n\t}\n\n\tret := *rc\n\treturn &ret\n}\n\nfunc (rc *ResourceInstanceChange) Moved() bool {\n\treturn !rc.Addr.Equal(rc.PrevRunAddr)\n}\n\n// Simplify will, where possible, produce a change with a simpler action than\n// the receiever given a flag indicating whether the caller is dealing with\n// a normal apply or a destroy. This flag deals with the fact that Terraform\n// Core uses a specialized graph node type for destroying; only that\n// specialized node should set \"destroying\" to true.\n//\n// The following table shows the simplification behavior:\n//\n//\tAction    Destroying?   New Action\n//\t--------+-------------+-----------\n//\tCreate    true          NoOp\n//\tDelete    false         NoOp\n//\tReplace   true          Delete\n//\tReplace   false         Create\n//\n// For any combination not in the above table, the Simplify just returns the\n// receiver as-is.\nfunc (rc *ResourceInstanceChange) Simplify(destroying bool) *ResourceInstanceChange {\n\tif destroying {\n\t\tswitch rc.Action {\n\t\tcase Delete:\n\t\t\t// We'll fall out and just return rc verbatim, then.\n\t\tcase CreateThenDelete, DeleteThenCreate:\n\t\t\treturn &ResourceInstanceChange{\n\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n\t\t\t\tDeposedKey:   rc.DeposedKey,\n\t\t\t\tPrivate:      rc.Private,\n\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr,\n\t\t\t\tChange: The actions during apply must be described entirely by\n\t// the Changes field, regardless of how the plan was created.\n\t//\n\t// FIXME: destroy operations still rely on DestroyMode being set, because\n\t// there is no other source of this information in the plan. New behavior\n\t// should not be added based on this flag, and changing the flag should be\n\t// checked carefully against existing destroy behaviors.\n\tUIMode Mode\n\n\t// VariableValues, VariableMarks, and ApplyTimeVariables together describe\n\t// how Terraform should decide the input variable values for the apply\n\t// phase if this plan is to be applied.\n\t//\n\t// VariableValues and VariableMarks describe persisted (non-ephemeral)\n\t// values that were set as part of the planning options and are to be\n\t// re-used during the apply phase. VariableValues can potentially contain\n\t// unknown values for a speculative plan, but the variable values must\n\t// all be known for a plan that will subsequently be applied.\n\t//\n\t// ApplyTimeVariables retains the names of any ephemeral variables that were\n\t// set (non-null) during the planning phase and must therefore be\n\t// re-supplied by the caller (potentially with different values) during\n\t// the apply phase. Ephemeral input variables are intended for populating\n\t// arguments for other ephemeral objects in the configuration, such as\n\t// provider configurations. Although the values for these variables can\n\t// change between plan and apply, their \"nullness\" may not.\n\tVariableValues     map[string]DynamicValue\n\tVariableMarks      map[string][]cty.PathValueMarks\n\tApplyTimeVariables collections.Set[string]\n\n\tChanges           *ChangesSrc\n\tDriftedResources  []*ResourceInstanceChangeSrc\n\tDeferredResources []*DeferredResourceInstanceChangeSrc\n\tTargetAddrs       []addrs.Targetable\n\tForceReplaceAddrs []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\tBackend           Backend\n\n\t// Complete is true if Terraform considers this to be a \"complete\" plan,\n\t// which is to say that it includes a planned action (even if no-op)\n\t// for every resource instance object that was mentioned across both\n\t// the desired state and prior state.\n\t//\n\t// If Complete is false then the plan might still be applyable (check\n\t// [Plan.Applyable]) but after applying it the operator should be reminded\n\t// to plan and apply again to hopefully make more progress towards\n\t// convergence.\n\t//\n\t// For an incomplete plan, other fields of this type may give more context\n\t// about why the plan is incomplete, which a UI layer could present to\n\t// the user as part of a warning that the plan is incomplete.\n\tComplete bool\n\n\t// Applyable is true if both Terraform was able to create a plan\n\t// successfully and if the plan calls for making some sort of meaningful\n\t// change.\n\t//\n\t// If [Plan.Errored] is also set then that means the plan is non-applyable\n\t// due to an error. If not then the plan was created successfully but found\n\t// no material differences between desired and prior state, and so\n\t// applying this plan would achieve nothing.\n\tApplyable bool\n\n\t// Errored is true if the Changes information is incomplete because\n\t// the planning operation failed. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01UnJwGFGREayDAtmf3gH5hs","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Building from Source\n     2→\n     3→Pre-built binaries are available for download for a variety of supported platforms through the [HashiCorp Releases website](https://releases.hashicorp.com/terraform/). \n     4→\n     5→However, if you'd like to build Terraform yourself, you can do so using the Go build toolchain and the options specified in this document.\n     6→\n     7→## Prerequisites\n     8→\n     9→1. Ensure you've installed the Go language version specified in [`.go-version`](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/main/.go-version).\n    10→2. Clone this repository to a location of your choice.\n    11→\n    12→## Terraform Build Options\n    13→\n    14→Terraform accepts certain options passed using `ldflags` at build time which control the behavior of the resulting binary.\n    15→\n    16→### Dev Version Reporting\n    17→\n    18→Terraform will include a `-dev` flag when reporting its own version (ex: 1.5.0-dev) unless `version.dev` is set to `no`:\n    19→\n    20→```\n    21→go build -ldflags \"-w -s -X 'github.com/hashicorp/terraform/version.dev=no'\" -o bin/ .\n    22→```\n    23→\n    24→### Experimental Features\n    25→\n    26→Experimental features of Terraform will be disabled unless `main.experimentsAllowed` is set to `yes`:\n    27→\n    28→```\n    29→go build -ldflags \"-w -s -X 'main.experimentsAllowed=yes'\" -o bin/ .\n    30→```\n    31→\n    32→In the official build process for Terraform, experiments are only allowed in alpha release builds. We recommend that third-party distributors follow that convention in order to reduce user confusion.\n    33→\n    34→## Go Options\n    35→\n    36→For the most part, the Terraform release process relies on the Go toolchain defaults for the target operating system and processor architecture.\n    37→\n    38→### `CGO_ENABLED`\n    39→\n    40→One exception is the `CGO_ENABLED` option, which is set explicitly when building Terraform binaries. For most platforms, we build with `CGO_ENABLED=0` in order to produce a statically linked binary. For MacOS/Darwin operating systems, we build with `CGO_ENABLED=1` to avoid a platform-specific issue with DNS resolution. \n    41→\n    42→\n    43→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01S3Nnapvpf6mqJAxs8KBcXx","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Building from Source\n     2→\n     3→Pre-built binaries are available for download for a variety of supported platforms through the [HashiCorp Releases website](https://releases.hashicorp.com/terraform/). \n     4→\n     5→However, if you'd like to build Terraform yourself, you can do so using the Go build toolchain and the options specified in this document.\n     6→\n     7→## Prerequisites\n     8→\n     9→1. Ensure you've installed the Go language version specified in [`.go-version`](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/main/.go-version).\n    10→2. Clone this repository to a location of your choice.\n    11→\n    12→## Terraform Build Options\n    13→\n    14→Terraform accepts certain options passed using `ldflags` at build time which control the behavior of the resulting binary.\n    15→\n    16→### Dev Version Reporting\n    17→\n    18→Terraform will include a `-dev` flag when reporting its own version (ex: 1.5.0-dev) unless `version.dev` is set to `no`:\n    19→\n    20→```\n    21→go build -ldflags \"-w -s -X 'github.com/hashicorp/terraform/version.dev=no'\" -o bin/ .\n    22→```\n    23→\n    24→### Experimental Features\n    25→\n    26→Experimental features of Terraform will be disabled unless `main.experimentsAllowed` is set to `yes`:\n    27→\n    28→```\n    29→go build -ldflags \"-w -s -X 'main.experimentsAllowed=yes'\" -o bin/ .\n    30→```\n    31→\n    32→In the official build process for Terraform, experiments are only allowed in alpha release builds. We recommend that third-party distributors follow that convention in order to reduce user confusion.\n    33→\n    34→## Go Options\n    35→\n    36→For the most part, the Terraform release process relies on the Go toolchain defaults for the target operating system and processor architecture.\n    37→\n    38→### `CGO_ENABLED`\n    39→\n    40→One exception is the `CGO_ENABLED` option, which is set explicitly when building Terraform binaries. For most platforms, we build with `CGO_ENABLED=0` in order to produce a statically linked binary. For MacOS/Darwin operating systems, we build with `CGO_ENABLED=1` to avoid a platform-specific issue with DNS resolution. \n    41→\n    42→\n    43→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_0191zqFFbh4f4WtiqjhNhb5Y","session_id":"28b04b2d-4c56-46ab-9f01-0f970d62835e","uuid":"18904c5a-6a31-43f2-8e1c-02ee2a905f61"}
